Letter Received

Letter from Roy Chapman Andrews 81

To the Editor:

The American Museum of Natural History in New York and the China Ancient Relics Preservation Committee have agreed on cooperation terms. With the permission of the Chinese government, passports have been issued for geological and paleontological research in Mongolia, with an equal number of specialists from China and the United States. Since departing at the end of April, we have been conducting research and exploration in the desert regions north of Zhangjiakou for over a thousand li. We have made significant discoveries in the strata of various eras and are continuing our work. The two specialists sent by the Chinese side are both experts in geology and paleontology, and the cooperation has been very satisfactory. However, a certain English newspaper recently published an article about my encounter with wolves on the journey, in which the wording regarding my Chinese colleagues was quite disrespectful. I was very surprised to read it. In fact, I have never met the reporter mentioned by the newspaper, and there is no way I could have had such a conversation. It may have been hearsay, with added imaginary words. If this causes any misunderstanding among my Chinese friends, I cannot be responsible and am very sorry. Encountering wolves and getting lost in the desert overnight are common occurrences for explorers. My Chinese colleagues and I have all taken it calmly and do not find it strange. I have already sent a letter to the original newspaper requesting a factual correction and telegraphed Shanghai to clarify. I would be grateful if you could publish this letter in your newspaper to avoid spreading false rumors. Sincerely, Roy Chapman Andrews.

Special Curfew in the City Today 82

The city's military and police authorities announced a special curfew after midnight last night, cutting off traffic. All district branches of the Public Security Bureau have increased patrols. Yesterday, they had already been preparing for the curfew in the areas bordering the Chinese territory and the concessions. Ministry of Finance Announces Regulations for Exchanging Military Reduction Bonds 83

To be handled in Shanghai starting September 1st.

The Ministry of Finance issued an announcement yesterday, stating: Announcement: In order to facilitate the circulation of the 1929 Military Reduction Bonds, the Ministry has approved the exchange of 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan, and 5 yuan tickets of the bonds for 1,000 yuan tickets. The regulations have been drafted and will be implemented starting September 1st at the Shanghai Bond Sales Office of the Ministry of Finance at the Jiangsu Bank on Jiangxi Road. The aforementioned regulations are hereby published in the newspaper for public information. Attached: Regulations of the Ministry of Finance for exchanging 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan, and 5 yuan tickets of the 1929 Military Reduction Bonds for 1,000 yuan tickets. 1. In order to facilitate circulation, the Ministry of Finance approves the exchange of 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan, and 5 yuan tickets of these bonds for 1,000 yuan tickets. The Shanghai Bond Sales Office is responsible for handling the exchange. 2. The Ministry of Finance has already printed 1,000 original 10,000 yuan tickets of these bonds, totaling 10,000,000 yuan in face value; 200,000 10 yuan tickets, totaling 2,000,000 yuan in face value; and 200,000 5 yuan tickets, totaling 1,000,000 yuan in face value. After deducting the winning tickets from the first, second, and third drawings, there are a total of 11,050,000 yuan in remaining tickets for the three types. 13,000 1,000 yuan tickets have been specially printed, numbered from A00001 to A13000. After separately extracting and destroying the bond tickets with already-winning numbers, the remaining 11,050 tickets, totaling 11,050,000 yuan in face value, are available for ticket holders to exchange. 3. The Ministry of Finance will publish a notice in the newspaper informing all ticket holders that they may exchange one 10,000 yuan ticket for ten 1,000 yuan tickets at any time within the prescribed period, or they may exchange multiple 10 yuan or 5 yuan tickets to make up a face value of 1,000 yuan and exchange it for one 1,000 yuan ticket. 4. For each 1,000 yuan ticket exchanged for 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan, or 5 yuan tickets, a printing fee of 2.50 silver dollars will be charged. 5. The manager of the exchange office should send a letter to the Central Bank of China and the Bank of Communications in various locations, requesting that if there are ticket holders requesting an exchange, they should promptly send the tickets to Shanghai for processing. In addition to paying the printing fee as required, the ticket holder should also pay postage fees. 6. The manager of the exchange office should create a detailed list of the amount of tickets exchanged each day and submit it to the Ministry of Finance for review. 7. The manager of the exchange office should punch holes in and invalidate the 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan, and 5 yuan tickets received each day, and after registering the last two digits of the number, send them to the Fund Management Committee for safekeeping. After they are collected, the Ministry of Finance will send personnel to re-count and destroy them. 8. If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Ministry of Finance may add or amend them at any time.

Far East Quarantine Inspection Group, Including Burke, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 84

Today Accompanied by Wu Liande to Japan

The Da Wan Bao reported that the Far East Port Quarantine Inspection Group arrived in Shanghai this morning (the 31st) on the President Taft. Its leader is Dr. Burke, who was originally the chief of port quarantine for Australia and was loaned to the Health Section of the League of Nations. He was sent to China by the League of Nations and worked with members of the Ministry of Health of the National Government to investigate the quarantine situation in various ports and assisted Dr. Wu Liande in formulating new port quarantine regulations. Therefore, he is very knowledgeable about the port quarantine situation in this port. He told reporters that the method of disinfecting ships used in Shanghai is of great interest to the group because it is different from that used in other ports in the Far East. Shanghai uses the German method of burning bone charcoal to produce a deadly poisonous gas that suffocates rats hiding in the ship's hold. Other ports in the Far East, according to the investigation, mostly use sulfur dioxide and hydrocyanic acid gas. The above three methods each have special value, so it is necessary to compare them. The Health Committee of the League of Nations is currently paying attention to the method of disinfecting cargo holds and has sent new members to specialize in this matter, so the group members attach great importance to it. He also said that the trip of the group is very beneficial and the interest is extremely high. They have already inspected ports in the Dutch East Indies, British Straits Settlements, French Vietnam, Hong Kong, Manila, and Guangzhou. Tomorrow (the 1st), they will leave Shanghai for Japan, and Dr. Wu Liande will also go with them. Japan is the last inspection site of the group. After completing the inspection, a meeting will be held in Japan to discuss the situation seen in various places in order to improve the situation. It is reported that the group was organized by the Health Section of the League of Nations so that health administrators in the Far East ports could send experts to compare the methods and procedures used in their ports with those in other ports, promote progress, and provide an opportunity for health administrators in various ports to get to know each other. After the group members arrived in Shanghai this morning, Dr. Wu Liande and others went to the dock to meet them and accompanied them to Dr. Wu's office in the Jianghai Customs Building. They were received by Minister Liu of the Ministry of Health, who delivered a welcome speech. At noon, Dr. Wu Liande hosted a banquet for the group members at the Dongya Restaurant. After the banquet, he accompanied them to visit various places along the Huangpu River and the Wusong Quarantine Station. In the evening, Minister Liu of the Ministry of Health hosted a banquet at the Dahua Hotel to welcome the group members.

Concession Telephone Company to be Transferred Today 85

The International Company will Take Over Management Starting Today

The Municipal Council of the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession held a meeting yesterday afternoon to make a final review of the case of the sale of the China and Foreign Telephone Company to the International Company. The resolution was forwarded by the Chairman to the Board of Directors of the Telephone Company and the International Company. Location is the Anti-Smuggling Department of the Ministry of Finance

Public Security Bureau Orders Issuance of Household Registration Forms for Signing 89

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau issued an order yesterday, stating that the city's household registration has been in place for over a year, and the number of households and various personnel registrations have gradually become accurate. It is urgently necessary to carry out analysis and statistics to serve as the standard for administrative facilities. Seven types of analytical statistics forms have been specially prescribed, and the statistics tags have been uniformly revised. The forms and tags have been printed in advance and distributed to each district director, who is ordered to instruct household registration patrol officers and police chiefs to comply with the order. Starting from July of this year, according to the items listed in each form, they should be carefully compiled and calculated by category. Each month, the forms should be filled out, attached to the household registration change statistics forms, compiled into a book, and submitted together for separate review and calculation. As for the prescribed forms and tags, they have been printed by the bureau and should be collected back. This is an important matter of government and should not be neglected. The order is given.

Social Affairs Bureau Orders Cessation of Wusong Chamber of Commerce Meeting 90

City Chamber of Commerce Informs Compliance

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau believes that Wusong is a commercial group in the city area and should be unified. Yesterday, it specially ordered the City Chamber of Commerce to stop the Wusong Chamber of Commerce from holding a meeting. After receiving the order from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Wusong Chamber of Commerce for reference. The original letter read: To Whom It May Concern: Our Chamber of Commerce previously reported that your Chamber of Commerce had a regularly scheduled reorganization. At that time, the Wusong Town had already been approved by the former Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association and the Social Affairs Bureau to establish a branch office. Subsequently, although your Chamber of Commerce stated that it had resolved not to establish a branch office, the Social Affairs Bureau still forwarded the original letter to the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association for review. On June 21st, the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce Members' Representative Conference convened by the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association still passed the motion to establish a branch office of the Wusong City Chamber of Commerce. Therefore, the original plan of the Social Affairs Bureau to approve Wusong's reorganization and establishment of a branch office of the City Chamber of Commerce has not been explicitly changed. The matter of whether your Chamber of Commerce's reorganization has been approved by the competent authorities is under review by the Social Affairs Bureau. Today, the 30th of this month, the Social Affairs Bureau approved the report, stating: Upon review, it is found that the Wusong Chamber of Commerce has previously submitted a report stating that it should not be reorganized into a branch office of the City Chamber of Commerce and requesting that a letter be forwarded to the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association to withdraw the agreement. The bureau has already forwarded the matter to the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association for reply, but has not yet received a reply. Now that the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Association has ended, since the matter has been resolved by the Members' Representative Conference, it should be promptly and truthfully reported to comply with procedures. It is claimed that the foregoing situation should be approved to the Chamber of Commerce to promptly prevent the Wusong Chamber of Commerce from holding a meeting without authorization and to report the handling of the matter as required. The order has been sent to the Chamber of Commerce to stop the regularly scheduled reorganization of your Chamber of Commerce and to await instructions from the competent authorities for handling.

The Labor Dispute of French-Owned Water and Electricity Workers Is Still Difficult to Resolve 94

The labor dispute of French-owned water and electricity workers has been delayed until now for forty days. According to the news from various meetings yesterday, it seems difficult to resolve for a while. The resolutions of the various meetings are recorded below:

General Meeting: Yesterday at 3 pm, a general meeting of members was held, with more than 500 people attending. Zhang Qixiang chaired the meeting. He first reported that yesterday (ie the day before yesterday), Li Shizeng of the Central Committee and Chen Junyi of the Municipal Committee notified them to send workers' representatives to negotiate and mediate. Wu Chunlin, Shen Keming, Zhu Xingen, and Zheng Ruisheng were appointed as representatives. Du Yuesheng represented the capitalists. Those present included Li Shizeng, Wang Xingzhou, a special commissioner of the Central Party Department, Geng Jiaji, secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Government, and Chen Junyi of the Municipal Party Department. As a result, the factory must dismiss two union-responsible workers, Xu A'mei and Zhang A'mao. The workers were extremely angry when they heard the news and unanimously denied it, insisting to the end. Then, Xu A'mei reported that the company staff voluntarily donated 147 yuan and 58 jiao in small coins to the Machinery Department to help the workers' lives. A resolution was passed on the following important matters: 1) The factory was warned not to dismiss any worker after resuming work, otherwise, they would strike again. 2) Those employees who do not report to the meeting will be dealt with severely.

Staff Meeting: The meeting was held at 10 am, chaired by Xu Tingliang, with more than 160 staff attending. The following important matters were resolved: 1) The outside staff of the Vehicle Department elected two temporary executive committee members to assist in all the association's affairs, namely Pan Changlin and Wu Jinrong, and two staff members of the Propaganda Department, namely Chen Guohua and Xu Xiuping. 2) Employees who join the association and are absent without reason will have their salaries deducted according to the number of days of absence after the resumption of work, which will be used as the association's public funds.

Backing Committee Meeting: The Backing Committee convened an emergency meeting yesterday, chaired by Hu Shouqi. The following important matters were resolved: 1) A resolution was passed to convene a regular representative meeting of various trade unions on August 3 at 2 pm. 2) Donation books will be printed and distributed to major trade unions, asking them to undertake fundraising. 3) A letter will be sent to the French water and electricity strike committee to organize a fundraising team and listen to the guidance of this association to go to various trade unions to raise donations. 4) A resolution was passed that this association should organize a fundraising guidance team and handed over to the fundraising department to be responsible for handling it. 5) It was secretly decided to send an international propaganda message in writing through the International Labour Office. 6) A resolution was passed to publish a declaration against the dismissal of workers. 7) It was secretly decided that this association should submit opinions and suggestions to Mr. Li Shizeng of the Central Committee on the key points to resolve the labor dispute. 8) A resolution was passed to submit a request to the municipal department to forward it to the central government to quickly resolve the July 21st tragedy in order to extend national rights.

Coal Industry Labor Dispute 95

Should Comply with the Main Text of the Arbitration Award

The coal industry labor dispute in this city. In April of this year, both parties submitted amendments to the agreement conditions. After the Municipal Party Department completed the review, it was sent to the Mediation Committee to convene mediation. The two parties were able to agree on most of the content of the conditions. However, the wage condition was insisted on, and the related rest days and meal and vegetable porridge items could not be decided. Therefore, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau requested the Municipal Government to submit it to the Arbitration Council for legal arbitration. However, the capitalists suddenly held different opinions and requested a retrial. However, the Municipal Government believed that the main text of the Council's arbitration award was extremely fair, so it issued an instruction yesterday, saying, "I have been informed. It is found that the 48 companies in the industry that went bankrupt were either due to meager capital or the influence of Jin Gui, which were difficult to maintain. They have their own legitimate reasons for bankruptcy. It cannot be said that they are all damages caused by wage issues. The proposed increase in income and reduction in expenditure is of course an important plan, but at a time when social life continues to increase, the living problems of workers should also be taken into account. The Arbitration Council instructed the capitalists of the industry to increase wages by 5%, and rejected the workers' request for 25 cents. The rest should still be handled in accordance with the original agreement between the two parties. Therefore, the arbitration award is as fair as the main text. The request for a retrial has no express provision in law, and it is difficult to approve it. You should comply with the arbitration award and implement it quickly. Do not delay it, lest it cause inconvenience. This is the approval."

Japanese Goods Transported to China Increases Again 97

The import of piece goods has improved, and the low silver price has caused Japanese goods to come to Shanghai. After a temporary decline, the transport of Japanese goods to Shanghai has been very crowded in recent weeks, with piece goods and foreign cloth accounting for the most. The Japanese Post Office sends six special ships for transport, and each ship has more than 2,000 pieces of cloth. The second largest is Dongtang, with 7,000 to 8,000 bags each time. The Yangtze River is the main route for going out. The ones used by the people on this street are more than doubled compared to last month. The Japanese Post Office also intends to add ships and increase transport.

Dispatching Personnel to Investigate Chinese Eels: The Aichi Prefecture Agricultural Association in Japan is currently building an eel farm with 800,000 yuan. The yellow sea eel and Bohai eel species in China are considered the best, and it has been decided to use this species. Currently, the

Aichi Prefecture Fisheries Department has also sent ten special commissioners, technicians, etc. to cross the Yellow Sea to Shanghai to conduct on-site inspections and research, and purchase eel species for breeding in Japan.

Shaanxi's Recent Disaster Situation and Relief Efforts 106

Report Obtained by Jisheng Society

According to Mr. Mou, a member of the Jisheng Society in China, who returned to Ji from Shaanxi, the disaster situation in Shaanxi is getting more and more serious every day. The following are a few points that the relief workers and others actually investigated and witnessed: 1) The situation is not stable, and banditry is rampant everywhere. Except for the hundreds of miles around Xi'an City, the roads are blocked everywhere. Even if you risk going to donate money, it is impossible to transport and send it. 2) The counties are harassed by bandits, and there is no pure land. The counties of a certain place are the most affected. People are fleeing, and the fields are barren. There is no seed to plant, and there is no harvest. The number of deaths is actually one-third. The situation is really unimaginable. 3) This association has witnessed that the disaster in Shaanxi is getting worse and worse, and the number of deaths is increasing. Due to various difficulties, relief efforts cannot be carried out. I have no choice but to change the establishment of refugee camps for disaster victims in Xi'an, Xianyang, Xingping, Wugong, Fufeng, and Qishan, and refugee camps for disaster-stricken children. There are eight places in total, each accommodating hundreds of people every year. The counties where the land can be cultivated only account for 30% to 40% of the province. Only the old, weak, women and children remain. The strong are flowing and becoming bandits. Young women are trafficked out of the country. Disaster victims and disaster-stricken children have no home to return to, and there is no end to the withdrawal of the camp. Each camp spends money every month, and the funds are insufficient. 4) Director Zhang of Wugong and Pingdeng Counties and all the relief workers personally went to transport and release funds for relief, and experienced dangers. Fortunately, they all turned danger into safety. After observing the situation, it is difficult to handle. There is only an urgent plan to cure the symptoms and set up shelters to avoid filling the ditches. In this way, we have to compromise, take risks, and do our best. We have to be based on conscience and save a life if we can. All of these are the personal experiences of the relief workers in Shaanxi. Natural disasters and man-made disasters are rare throughout the ages, and it is difficult to convey the tragedy in face-to-face conversations and writing.

Meeting of the Public Works Department's Transportation Committee 112

Permanent Provisions for One-Way Traffic on Hankou Road

At 4:30 pm on July 21st, the Public Works Department held a meeting of the Transportation Committee. Those present included Mr. Braun, Mr. Chen Tingrui, Mr. Macnaughten, Mr. Okamoto, the Additional Minister of the Police Department, and the General Office. The matters discussed were as follows: "Election of Chairman" proposed by Mr. Braun, seconded by Mr. Chen Tingrui, and Mr. Hepie was elected as Chairman. In his absence, Mr. Macnaughten acted as Chairman, which was approved by all. The minutes of the previous meeting were approved and signed by the members. "One-Way Traffic Rules": 1) Hankou Road: The trial period for one-way traffic on Hankou Road has now expired. This measure not only has a significant effect on the road, but also has a positive impact on the roads in the Central District and the Zhabei District. According to statistics, the number of vehicles traveling on Hankou Road in the three months since then is more frequent than in the past, while the number of accidents has been less. Therefore, the Director of the Police Department proposed that the measure should be made a permanent rule, so that traffic within the concession can be reduced. A month ago, the Chinese Ratepayers Association and other sectors within the concession sent letters to protest against the measure. After reviewing it, the Director of the Police Department revised the daily specified time as follows: from west to east, 8:00 am to 9:00 am, 1:00 pm to 2:00 pm; from east to west, 12:00 noon to 1:00 pm, 4:30 pm to 5:30 pm. All the members agreed that since the measure has achieved positive results on Hankou Road, they unanimously agreed to the proposal of the Director of the Police Department to make it a permanent rule, and also agreed to the revised time. 2) Yuanmingyuan Road: Mr. Martin, the Additional Minister of the Police Department, reported on the case of the trial one-way traffic on the road, saying that the Traffic Section had reviewed the case in detail. It was found that since the trial one-way traffic on the road, there had been no good results. It is not appropriate to continue this measure and it should be revoked immediately. However, in order to improve the current situation, it is stipulated that vehicles on the road can only be parked on the west side of the road at a certain number of points to avoid disorder. Prebendary Stevens has sent a letter to the Bureau, stating the various inconveniences that have occurred since the implementation of one-way traffic on the road. The letter was submitted to the committee for discussion, and the result was unanimous agreement to cancel this regulation. "Banning of Street Vendors": There are often many street vendors gathered on the west side of Nanjing Road and Tibet Road, which often obstructs vehicle traffic. The presiding officer proposed that it should be prohibited. It was resolved that the case should be handled by the Additional Minister of the Police Department and a notice should be issued to prohibit street vendors from gathering on the side of the road to facilitate traffic. The meeting adjourned at 4:50.

First Batch of New Tea to Be Shipped to Russia Today 113

Since the Soviet Russian Commercial Fleet resumed the Vladivostok route, this year the Soviet Union has sent a committee to Shanghai to purchase and transport Chinese tea. The first batch can be shipped out today. The details of the purchase are recorded below:

Restoration of the Sino-Russian Cooperative Association: The Soviet Russian tea procurement agency in China is located in Shanghai and is named the Sino-Russian Cooperative Association. It specializes in purchasing Chinese tea leaves and packing them to Russia. When the two countries severed diplomatic relations last year, the cooperative association was closed and suspended its business, and the people in charge left Shanghai and returned to Russia, entrusting the British firm Jinlong to handle the unfinished business. Now that Sino-Russian shipping has resumed and trade between the two countries has also opened, the Moscow Cooperative Association has sent the original staff to Shanghai to restore the Shanghai branch. It has established an office at No. 2 Beijing Road and has notified various tea merchants to start handling goods and restoring the situation before the severance of diplomatic relations.

The first batch of new tea is shipped out: The new Chinese tea purchased by the cooperative association is mainly green tea and tea bricks. At the same time, Jinlong purchased a batch of new tea bricks on behalf of Russian merchants. The total of the two is more than 1,100 tons, which is entrusted to the Soviet Russian Commercial Team. The Roundland commercial ship chartered by Laisi Foreign Company in Shanghai will be loaded and exported to Vladivostok today. This is the first batch of goods to be shipped to Russia after the new tea was launched this year.

Agricultural Products Inspection Office Ordered to Inspect Imported Foreign Bees 117

In recent years, the domestic beekeeping industry has become increasingly developed, with Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces having the most beekeeping. Most of the bee species are purchased from abroad, with the Italian species being the most imported, followed by the British and American species. When the price is high, each box reaches more than 30 yuan. Foreigners compete to import them for profit, and sell them with inferior bee species. When importing, the customs does not inspect them. Now the Ministry of Agriculture has ordered the Agricultural Products Inspection Office in this city to conduct strict inspections of imported foreign bee species in the future to benefit agriculture. After receiving the order, the office immediately prepared the inspection procedures and will send personnel to implement the inspection after contacting the Jianghai Customs.

Where Did the Fake Promissory Note Come From? 123

Lu Zhaoshun Arrested by Police

Chen Yunfu, from Yuyao, operates the Rui Tai Silk Thread Shop at No. 472 Near Guan Bridge on Limalu in the South City. He has been in business for many years and is quite prosperous. Around 8 PM the night before last, Chen happened to be out. Suddenly, a man, about thirty years old and well-dressed, arrived at the shop. The staff recognized him as a customer and served him. The man took out a promissory note purportedly issued by the shop, worth sixty yuan, and asked to redeem it for cash. Upon inspection by the staff, it was indeed a Rui Tai promissory note. While they were discussing it, Chen returned to the shop and, after reading it, determined that there was no such note in the company's records. After a detailed investigation, it was discovered that the seal on the note was forged, making it a clear case of fraudulent redemption. They immediately called the police on duty in the area and questioned the man about his origins. The man appeared flustered and was immediately taken to the First District Police Station. The district chief ordered a preliminary interrogation, during which the man identified himself as Lu Zhaoshun. His other statements were evasive. The district chief, considering it a criminal case involving private seal engraving and fraudulent redemption of money with fake notes, ordered that he be transferred to the Shanghai Superior Court for investigation and legal action.

The merchants and educational circles in the town, led by Yang Xinzheng, have initiated a free clinic every summer, employing famous Shanghai doctors such as Wang Bingjun to provide consultations and vaccinations every two and seven days of the month. The clinic is located in the Chenghuang Temple in the central market of Caohejing Town and began providing consultations today. The nearby villagers are full of praise.

Hu Deguang and Ye Guorui Declared Not Guilty 125

Hu Deguang, a shop assistant, and Ye Guorui, an apprentice, at the Jiashun pawnshop in Caojiadu, West Shanghai, were accused by the shop owner, Xiao Xueming, of stealing ninety-one pieces of jewelry in March of this year. After several trials at the Criminal Court of the District Court, they were declared not guilty at the end of last month due to a lack of evidence. The court's judgment is excerpted below: (Main text) Ye Guorui and Hu Deguang are both not guilty. The attached civil lawsuit is dismissed. (Facts) Ye Guorui and Hu Deguang were both employees at the Jiashun pawnshop opened by Xiao Xueming in Caojiadu. Ye Guorui also managed the key to the jewelry box. On March 22nd, the shop discovered that ninety-one pieces of jewelry were missing from the jewelry box. On the 20th, Xiao Xueming's wife heard a noise in the shop around 2 AM. Additionally, Hu Deguang was seen giving Ye Guorui a package containing "Hagao" (a type of cake) to give to someone on the morning of the 22nd, leading to suspicion that Ye Guorui and Hu Deguang were jointly involved in the theft. Xiao Xueming filed a lawsuit, and the prosecutor of this court investigated and prosecuted. In the attached civil lawsuit, the plaintiff also requested the court to order the defendants to compensate for losses of 800 yuan. (Reasoning) The establishment of facts should be based on evidence. This is the principle of criminal procedure law. The theft of jewelry from Xiao Xueming's pawnshop, suspecting Ye Guorui and Hu Deguang of jointly stealing, is based on the fact that the key on the night of the 20th was in the custody of Ye Guorui and was not handed over upstairs. (Omission) Based on the above discussion and conclusion, the criminal suspicion of the defendants cannot be proven, and they should be declared not guilty in accordance with Article 316 of the Criminal Procedure Law. The attached civil lawsuit should also be dismissed. The judgment is made as stated in the main text.

Water Police Kidnapping Case Demands 70,000 Yuan Ransom 132

Suspects Tried Yesterday

Chen Guoliang, a squad leader of the 17th team of the 4th District of the Wusong Water Police stationed at Dingxing Sand, opposite Wusongkou; Zhang Liujin, the team leader; Wang Youcai; and five bandits dressed as military officers conspired to kidnap Wang Buyun, the head of the sand village, his son, Shi Yongshun (also known as Shi Xiaowa), the owner of the fishing line at Shitousha, and five others including Mr. Gong. Details have been reported in this newspaper. After the incident, Captain Gong sent personnel to arrest two suspects and interrogated them in the district. Yesterday, Shi Jiacheng, the son of Shi Yongshun, received a letter from the kidnappers stating that Wang Buyun and others were in Chenjiasha, Lusi, Jiangbei. They demanded 30,000 yuan for Shi Yongshun, 10,000 yuan for Wang Buyun and his son, and 30,000 yuan for the Gong family, totaling 70,000 yuan. They demanded the money be prepared within a week for negotiation and ransom, or they would resort to drastic measures. Shi Jiacheng, upon reading the letter, found the ransom too large to raise. He stated that his father, Shi Yongshun, had suffered multiple robberies and kidnappings in recent years, resulting in significant debts that he could not repay. He would have to leave it to fate.

Also, the suspects, Officer Huang, and water police officers Gong Xibao, Wang Luncai, Zhou Chongquan, and Peng Jie, were interrogated by presiding judge Zhang Wei of the county at 1 PM yesterday. Officer Huang Yutang stated that he was 48 years old, from Jiujiang. He supervised squad leader Gong Xibao, Chen Guoliang, and water police officers Wang Luncai, Zhou Chongquan, Peng Jie, Zhang Liujin, and Wang Youcai stationed at Ruifengsha. One day before the incident, a man in uniform came to the sand and visited squad leader Chen Guoliang, staying overnight. The next morning, when he left, Huang asked Chen who the visitor was, and Chen said it was an acquaintance from Haimen who had come to gamble. Later, around 2 PM, six more people came to visit Chen and talk, and then left shortly after. Huang was suspicious and asked about their background. Chen said they were all friends from Haimen working in a certain department there. They reported to him that outsiders suspected him of illegal activities. Huang told Chen that as long as he worked honestly and diligently, there would be no slander. Later, Huang and Gong went out on patrol, and unexpectedly, Chen coerced his brothers to hand over their guns and, together with Zhang Liujin and Wang Youcai, escaped and kidnapped people, which was unexpected. Squad leader Gong Xibao stated that he was 32 years old and that he was not aware of Chen Guoliang's collusion with bandits and had no relationship with him. Wang Luncai stated that he was 32 years old, from Qidong, and served as a squad member in the 17th team of the 4th District. He was unaware of Chen's collusion with bandits. When Chen forced them to hand over their weapons, Huang and Gong were on duty outside. He repeatedly pleaded with Chen and was not dragged away. Zhou Chongquan stated that he was 20 years old, from Chongming. On the day of the incident, Chen ordered him and his companions to put on their uniforms and carry their guns, thinking they were going on patrol. Chen instructed them to go to a certain place to kidnap people. He repeatedly begged to be excused, but his gun was taken away, and he knew nothing else. Peng Jie stated that he was 23 years old, from Anhui. After Huang and Gong went out, Chen immediately called them to put on their uniforms and set off with him, saying that they would not return. They found Chen's words strange and refused to go, which made Chen very angry. He took away their guns and bullets. When they spoke, Chen drew his gun and threatened them to go with him. They were terrified and fled to nearby homes to hide. However, Zhang Jinliu and Wang Youcai were still forced to go with him, and he knew nothing else, asking for leniency. Later, the victims' families arrived and stated that they did not see these five people during the incident. After reviewing the statements, Zhang ordered Huang and others to be taken back into custody pending further investigation. He also reported to County Chief Qiu, ordering his subordinates to assist the 4th District Water Police in arresting Chen Guoliang and others, investigating and prosecuting them, and finding out the whereabouts of the hostages for rescue.

Zhang Wenqing's Appeal on the Case of Conspiring to Kill His Step-Mother Concludes with Debate 133

The Prosecutor Requests to Uphold the Original Judgment

Judgment Scheduled for August 6th

At 9 AM yesterday, the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court continued the hearing on the case of Zhang Wenqing conspiring with others to kill his stepmother, allowing lawyers from both sides to make oral arguments. First, Zhang Wenqing's lawyer argued that the evidence in this case was based on the appellant's repeated confessions. Regarding the confession made in the police station, whether that confession could be adopted should be studied. According to the provisions of the Criminal Procedure Law, a confession that can be used as evidence must be true and voluntarily stated. During the initial trial, Zhang confessed that after being detained in the police station, the detectives told him that if he confessed, he would be released, otherwise, he would be tortured. The confession made in the police station was coerced and should not be adopted. Zhang also said that the police station presented his confession form, which was written by the police personnel in advance and only asked him to sign it. Zhang, who knew how to read and write, should have written the confession form himself. If someone else wrote it on his behalf, it could not be used as evidence. Furthermore, the confessions of the other appellants were contradictory. For example, Yao Yonggui said he arrived at Zhang's house at 5 PM, while Gao Jintang said it was 2 PM. Regarding the reward, some said it was 500 yuan, some said 400 yuan, and some said 100 yuan. Such confessions should not be adopted. The confessions examined by this court may be credible because Chen Hengcai has now rediscovered his conscience and admitted that he alone killed Ms. Su. Although Chen, Yao, and Gao all said that when they entered Zhang's house, Zhang Wenqing was waiting on the escalator, this statement seems to be premeditated, but it actually shows Zhang's honest heart. If he was indeed an accomplice, he would not have waited there but would have avoided it early on. Chen Hengcai did this because he had borrowed 40 yuan from Su, and Su repeatedly demanded it back, leading Chen to develop malicious intent. After Su was injured and admitted to the hospital, Zhang still visited her and gave her medicine, showing that he had no intention of killing her. Therefore, Zhang was actually implicated and should be declared not guilty. Another lawyer for Zhang, Jiang Rong, supplemented the arguments made by the previous lawyer, Wang Chuanbi, stating that Chen killed Su partly for money and partly for some other relationship, which had nothing to do with Zhang. Then, Chen Hengcai's lawyer, Fan Gang, defended that Chen had already confessed to killing Su, but it was not intentional. Because Su repeatedly demanded the debt without success, she stabbed Chen with a knife, and Chen disarmed Su and accidentally stabbed her to death. This was unintentional and cannot be said to be premeditated. Lawyers Wang Shizong and Chao Kun also defended Yao Yonggui, stating that Chen Hengcai invited Yao Yonggui to Zhang's house, only knowing that he was going to play and not knowing about the murder. Yao did not strike a blow. It is difficult to recognize that Yao committed a crime. Gao Jintang was defended pro bono by lawyer Wu Zhiping, who stated that when Su was stabbed and admitted to the hospital, Chief Detective Hua went to inquire, and she said that Yao and Chen stabbed her. Su Xiaoting (Su's younger brother) also said at the hospital that Yao and Chen killed her, not mentioning Gao. Although Su's son said that Chen, Yao, and an unknown person killed his mother, this unknown person cannot be determined to be Gao. Gao should be declared not guilty. Then, the police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that the evidence of Zhang Wenqing and the other three's crimes was quite solid and requested the court to reject the appeal and uphold the original judgment. Finally, Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan stood up and expressed his opinion, stating that the facts of this case were extremely clear. After Chen, Yao, and Gao entered Zhang's house, they closed the back door, indicating that they had already planned it. The first defendant's defender, lawyer Wang Chuanbi, said that Zhang Wenqing was still waiting on the ladder when he saw Chen and others enter the room, showing that he was honest. However, this was not the case. When people have great hope, they often reveal their true feelings and forget their usual state. Zhang's waiting on the escalator was precisely when his hope was greatest. Judge Song then announced the end of the debate in this case and scheduled the verdict for the morning of August 6th.

Civil Servant Sues Over Loss of Money While Soliciting Prostitutes 134

Xu Xiangfei's Fall is Pitiful

Zhang Teng'an Stains Official Integrity

Xu Xiangfei, a woman from Suzhou residing at No. 1180 Siwenli, Xinzha Road, is still unmarried. She once studied at a church school in Beiping, but dropped out due to the decline of her family. Recently, she was forced to make a living and willingly degraded herself. As a former female student, she became a private prostitute, going to major hotels in the evening to solicit customers. On the evening of the 28th of last month, Xu went to the Oriental Hotel on Xizang Road and was seen by Zhang Teng'an, a traveler staying in Room 249 of the hotel. Zhang originally worked at the Jinling Customs and came to Shanghai on business. Feeling lonely in the hotel, he was amazed by Xu's beauty and inquired with the tea boy, learning that she was a prostitute and could be recruited with money. He called her into his room and asked her to share his pillow. Xu demanded ten gold coins for the night. They slept together until 3 AM, and then Xu went home. The next night, she went to see him again, and they found each other very agreeable. Xu borrowed two gold coins from Zhang. They talked until late at night before parting. After Xu left, Zhang reopened his wallet and found that the eighty yuan he had stored were gone. Zhang believed that since no third party had entered the room, Xu must have stolen the money. Fortunately, he knew the woman's location after spending two nights with her. He reported this to the Laozha Police Station, and Detective Huang Fusen arrested the woman the night before last. Yesterday, she was brought to the Special District District Court and interrogated by Judge Xu. The police station's lawyers, Gan Jingxian and Hu Jiabao, stated the case, and Zhang proved the circumstances of the theft. Xu Xiangfei confessed that she stayed with Zhang the first night and went to talk to him for a while the next night, then went to Room 55 to sit for a while until 11:30 PM. Zhang gave her two yuan to buy opium. She did not see Zhang's wallet and did not know where the wallet was placed. She returned home the next day because she could not get the opium and returned the two gold coins. At that time, she was suddenly accused of theft, which was a false accusation. After questioning, Judge Xu stated that Zhang, as a civil servant, had tainted his official integrity by soliciting prostitutes. Furthermore, there was no evidence to accuse her of theft. He sternly reprimanded Zhang, who could only agree. Xu Xiangfei was released in court because there was no basis for the accusation.

Zhang Aila Withdraws Lawsuit Against Zhao Jiabi 135

Judge Personally Drafts Correction

Advises Plaintiff Not to Be Too Demanding

The "Chinese Students Magazine," published by Liangyou Book Company, has been published for two years. Its content is upright, and the student community considers it a useful modern publication. The editor, Zhao Jiabi, is a young scholar, so the magazine sells well. Previously, an article titled "Analysis of the Incident of Throwing Oneself into the Dance Floor" written by Wang Yuanxing was published in the second issue, number 14, which Zhang Aila (Zipinlan), who had once been known as the queen of Fudan University, believed damaged her reputation. She filed a lawsuit against the magazine. After the initial trial on the 11th of last month, both parties followed the court's instructions to settle out of court. However, because the plaintiff had intentions of demanding more on the drafted conditions, presiding judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District District Court held a continued hearing yesterday morning. The defendant hired two lawyers, Chen Tingrui and Qian Baohe, to defend. The plaintiff's lawyer, Li Zhongdao, was not present in court. Miss Zhang herself arrived with two young men in Western suits one quarter of an hour before the start of the trial. First, lawyer Chen stated that the manuscript published in the "Chinese Students Magazine" was based on the "Following Bai Ying and Leaving" article in the "Republic Daily" and did not contain any defamatory words against Zhang. However, due to the court's earnest advice, they had settled. However, the plaintiff was still making many demands, which was excessive. Judge Cheng then questioned the plaintiff, "You agreed to the settlement conditions in court last time, why do you regret it now?" Zhang replied that she was not entirely satisfied with the wording of the manuscript to be published in the "Chinese Students Magazine." Judge Cheng asked, "What are you not satisfied with?" Zhang replied that it did not state the source of the photos. Judge Cheng asked, "Is that the only point?" Zhang nodded. Judge Cheng then drafted a correction, "According to Ms. Zhang, the photos were stolen without her consent. This is hereby declared." After Zhang read the correction, she requested that the letter from lawyer Li Zhongdao to the defendant's lawyer also be published in the magazine. It was heard that the letter mainly praised Zhang's virtues at school. The court considered her request unreasonable and did not approve it. Judge Cheng also advised Zhang, "The 'Chinese Students Magazine' edited by the defendant is a valuable publication in society, and the words it contains have not damaged your reputation. The defendant also did not intend to insult anyone, so this kind of lawsuit should be ended early. Why be so demanding? Are you satisfied with the proposed correction now?" Zhang then agreed, and Zhang voluntarily requested to withdraw the case.

Yesterday’s Court Hearing

None of the Defendants Appeared

Rescheduled for Tomorrow

The Municipal Council (工部局) considers that the sale of aphrodisiacs by merchants is increasing daily. If strict prohibition is not enforced, it will cause incalculable harm to the population. Therefore, in addition to restricting newspapers from publishing such advertisements, it is also investigating homes selling aphrodisiacs to prosecute them according to the law. It has now been ascertained that the following seven establishments secretly sell various aphrodisiacs: Ji Cang Pharmaceutical Company at 422 Labour Road, Aix Pharmacy at 14 Haikou Road, Zhongnan Pharmacy at 429 Fuzhou Road, Bailin Company at 179 Park Road, Gefang Congji Society at 111 North Shanxi Road, Zhongxi Department Store at 478 North Zhejiang Road (corner of Haining Road), and a certain pharmacy in the French Concession. The court approved the request. The day before yesterday, Chief Inspector Xue Zhiliang and Inspector Pan Linshi of the General Inspectorate searched each location. Except for the pharmacy in the French Concession, which could not be searched due to jurisdictional issues, the other six locations were found to have a large quantity of aphrodisiacs with various names, such as "Unyielding Might Pill," "Yang Strengthening Pill," "Kidney Tonifying Pill," "Kidney Tonifying Elixir," "Contraceptive Powder," "Mandarin Duck Powder," and "Quick Removal Powder," too numerous to list. The Zhongnan Pharmacy had the most diverse variety. The account books of each establishment were also seized and sent to the police station. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Shumu held a court hearing. None of the summoned Zhao Jicang and others appeared. Inspector Pan reported on the search process and stated that the Zhongnan Pharmacy had been selling aphrodisiacs for the longest time and profited the most. After newspapers disclosed the case of investigating aphrodisiac advertisements in newspapers a few days ago, the pharmacy anticipated the news and hid the prohibited drugs. Although the quantity seized yesterday was not large, the variety was the greatest in that pharmacy. Since all the defendants have not appeared, a postponement should be granted, he said. Judge Shen ordered the hearing to be rescheduled for this Saturday (tomorrow) to summon the defendants for questioning.

市府請示整理寺廟之權責 147

The Municipal Government Requests Instructions on the Authority and Responsibility of Organizing Temples

The Shanghai Municipal Government, formerly the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee, sent a letter to request the results of the registration of temple properties in the city, both registered and unregistered, in order to jointly organize the matter. The Municipal Government considered that the registration of municipal temples fell within the scope of administrative affairs, and the Temple Registration Regulations did not explicitly state that the Executive Committee should jointly organize it. Therefore, it specifically submitted a report to the Executive Yuan, asking for instructions on how to handle the matter and requesting a prompt review and approval. The report stated that the case involved the handling of municipal temples by party and government agencies, and requested instructions on how to divide the authority and responsibilities and requested a prompt review and approval. Previously, a letter was received from the Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang Shanghai Special City, stating that the temples in the city had been registered by your government in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the National Government. The outside world knows little about the results. At the beginning of this political training, such superstitious businesses should be properly handled. Therefore, we specifically request you to investigate and announce the results of the registration of all the temples in the city, both registered and unregistered, in order to jointly organize them. We hope to receive a reply. In response to this, the registration of temples by the government is based on current laws and regulations. According to Article 14 of the promulgated Temple Registration Regulations, after the registration is completed, the handling agency, the Special City Public Security Bureau, shall submit a register to the competent Special City Government for record. Article 15 states that a report shall be submitted to the Ministry of Internal Affairs every three months, etc. Inquiring into the intention of the legislation, there is no need for publication. Moreover, Article 10 of the same regulations briefly states that the registration of temples in the Special City is the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau. Also, Article 5 of the Regulations for Supervising Temples states that the property and legal items of temples shall be presented to the local government for registration, etc. It is clear that the handling of temples falls within the scope of administrative affairs, which is self-evident and needs no further explanation. Now, the city's Executive Committee requests to publish the registration case and jointly organize the temples, which is intended to eliminate superstition, and the government fully agrees with this. However, the work of political training has its own systems, and party-government cooperation also has its own responsibilities and powers. This time, the Executive Committee's proposed appropriate handling and joint organization of various sections, the government has no legal basis to follow. The question of how to handle this matter is reasonably combined to submit a document for your approval, which is really for the public convenience, etc.

Special Publication

兒童法院組織大綱 152

Outline of the Organization of Children's Courts

Proposed by the China Child Welfare Association

Children's Courts (Juvenile Courts) are *

Organizations specially established by civilized countries in modern times. The nature of juvenile delinquency is different from that of adult crime. It is inappropriate to send them to ordinary courts to be equated with ordinary adult criminals. The China Child Welfare Association has a Children's Protection Department, which has been working tirelessly to protect children. Recently, it has also drafted an outline for the organization of children's courts, which will be submitted to the National Government for adoption and implementation.

I. ㈠ The jurisdiction of the Children's Court extends to the following cases: (A) Crimes committed by children. Although the Chinese Criminal Law stipulates that the actions of people under the age of 13 are not punishable, and that people between the ages of 10 and 13 who commit crimes can be sent to reformatories, there are still many cases of juvenile delinquency that are not considered violations of the law by the Chinese Criminal Law, which really require the compulsory judgment of the Children's Court. For juvenile offenders, after interrogation by the Children's Court, they may be sent to vocational schools or charitable organizations. For children who have lost their parents, the Children's Court may temporarily adopt them. (B) Children's (

C) Improper conduct may be voluntarily submitted to the court by parents or other guardians. (C) Children who have been harmed, such as adults who have been accused of infringing on children, stealing children's belongings, selling or abusing slaves, and others, adults who incite children to commit crimes, fraudulently buying stolen goods from children, encouraging children to commit illegal acts, and others, adults who are unable to bear the responsibility of educating children, unable to send children to school, unable to provide children with medical care, and others, first send the adult who harmed the child to the Children's Court for questioning, and after restoring the losses of the harmed child, send the adult to the ordinary court for trial. (D) Divorce and separation cases involving children. Ordinary divorce and separation cases are naturally accepted by ordinary judicial organs, but the issues of child management and education must be transferred to the Children's Court for handling. (E) Regulations on the education and upbringing of illegitimate children. Judges may order the parents of illegitimate children to be responsible for the education and upbringing of their children. (F) Guardianship matters concerning children who are contrary to normal behavior. Contrary to normal behavior refers to those who are neurasthenic, intellectually weak, and have manic behavior. (G) Child labor cases, eliminating occupations that harm child labor, limiting the maximum working hours, prohibiting night work, and others. (H) Concerning orphans and abandonment, examining the economic conditions of their families, finding ways to provide children with medical care, and controlling their occupations and environment. ㈡ The jurisdiction of the Children's Court extends to all children under the age of sixteen, regardless of gender.

II. Organizational Law ㈠ Judges should be qualified professionals with a longer term of office to focus on service. Six years is generally the most appropriate. During their term of office, in addition to interrogating cases, they must also guide the work of the court. ㈡ Case Prosecution Department, (A) Each prosecutor cannot handle more than 50 cases at the same time. (B) Department members must be prudent in matters, verify qualifications, pass examinations, and their minimum qualifications must be a university degree or equivalent academic ability, or a graduate of social sciences, with at least one year of case research under supervision, and must have excellent personality and character, discernment, intelligence, and understanding. (C) The remuneration of prosecutors must be based on their performance. The salary level is roughly similar to that received by personnel in other social organizations. Salary increases must be based on their work performance and efficiency. ㈢ In the initial stage, the scope of the Children's Court is limited to the attached courts of the local court. ㈣ Recording system. Each court must have a recording system for compiling legal records and other records related to investigations and completed work. Various investigation records must contain the necessary facts of case studies in the active plan, in progress, and after success. At the same time, a chronology of supervisory affairs must be recorded. ㈤ Appraisers. Appraisers handle scientific or difficult events. ㈥ The application of case research and scientific methods, cooperating with courts in several case-free clinics, can collect case materials and various methods for treating transgressing children. This is a valuable reference based on the prevention of the future and the diagnosis of the past.

III. Procedural Law ㈠ The pre-trial judge or the prosecutor designated by the judge must review various lawsuits, add various political materials from the social aspect, and then decide whether it is necessary to formally file a lawsuit with the court. ㈡ Interrogation. Interrogation must be serious and accurate, and unnecessary publicity and rituals are generally exempted. ㈢ The definite plan for handling the case, although in this trial period, must also be clearly stipulated, and the chief prosecutor or other supervisor must check it together every month. Reporting at a reliable time is a valuable aid for inspection, but reporting is not a substitute for case research methods. The court shall find ways to collect laws and regulations on helpless people and illegitimate children, and when necessary, shall find ways to collect laws and regulations on wives' ransom.

Page 12

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education's Administrative Plan for the 19th Year, First Period (I) 153

The Ministry of Education's administrative plan for the first three-month period (July to September) of the 19th year is as follows:

Regarding Improving Higher Education:

(1) Reviewing the qualifications of new student admissions; (2) Issuing orders urging colleges and universities to submit overview reports for the 18th year; (3) Cracking down on schools that have prematurely changed their names to colleges or universities without approval; (4) Conducting qualification examinations for graduates and students of private colleges and universities that have been closed or have not yet been registered; (5) Issuing orders urging local academic groups to register and submit overview reports for the past year; (6) Reviewing the academic records of college and university graduates; (7) Organizing the lists of past graduates submitted by colleges and universities; (8) Organizing reports on summer hygiene training courses held in various regions; (9) Reviewing the academic performance of government-funded students studying in Japan; (10) Handling the registration of colleges and universities; (11) Continuing to crack down on substandard private colleges and universities; (12) Organizing a drafting committee for university curriculum standards and equipment standards.

Regarding Continuing the Work of Secondary Education:

(1) Completing and promulgating the curriculum standards for normal courses in senior high schools; (2) Completing and promulgating the curriculum standards for agriculture, industry, and commerce courses in senior high schools; (3) Drafting curriculum standards for home economics courses in senior high schools; (4) Drafting curriculum standards for rural normal schools; (5) Completing and issuing the statistical tables for each middle school and the statistical tables for secondary schools in each province and city for the 18th year; (6) Completing the format of various reporting forms for middle schools, to be implemented starting from the 19th year; (7) Completing and promulgating the outline for moral education in middle schools.

Regarding Planned Implementation of Secondary Education:

(1) Stipulating equipment standards for each subject in junior and senior high schools; (2) Stipulating standards for the allocation of recurring expenses in middle schools; (3) Stipulating methods for the appointment of middle school principals; (4) Stipulating methods for the salaries of middle school teachers and staff; (5) Stipulating methods for examinations in each subject in middle schools.

Regarding Improving Elementary Education:

(1) Printing and distributing promotional guidelines for the use of vernacular Chinese textbooks in elementary and junior high schools; (2) Continuing to compile a statistical report on the overview of national elementary education; (3) Continuing to investigate the forms currently used in elementary schools and kindergartens; (4) Continuing to plan for the improvement of local educational administrative organizations; (5) Stipulating methods for restricting experimental schools; (6) Issuing a notice restricting elementary schools from compiling their own textbooks and illustrations; (7) Stipulating an outline for moral education in elementary schools before the standards for moral education in elementary schools are stipulated, with special emphasis on eradicating bad habits inherited from the nation and cultivating good habits that are lacking in the people; (8) Formulating elementary school regulations and implementation details.

Regarding Implementing Compulsory Education:

(1) Establishing a Central Compulsory Education Committee (originally planned for the second period but not established, now planned for this period); (2) Compiling survey statistical forms on compulsory education for distribution and investigation; (3) Investigating the methods of compulsory education implementation in various countries.

Regarding Overseas Chinese Education:

(1) Allocating supplementary funds for overseas Chinese education (500,000 yuan annually, already approved by the National Government and included in the budget from the 19th year); (2) Consulting with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on establishing overseas Chinese education specialists in various overseas consulates; (3) Instructing various consuls to direct local overseas Chinese education associations and general school affairs associations to continue their efforts before the establishment of the overseas Chinese education association; (4) Instructing various consuls to encourage overseas Chinese education organizations to develop social education; (5) Compiling and promulgating regulations for overseas Chinese elementary schools.

Regarding Provincial, Municipal, and Local Educational Administration:

(1) Reviewing the administrative plans of the education departments and bureaus of each province and city, and guiding their work; (2) Urging the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to submit routine reports in a timely manner, and providing criticism and guidance; (3) Stipulating methods for the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to implement vocational guidance; (4) Reviewing the work of the education departments and bureaus of each province and city, selecting the best ones, and requesting the Executive Yuan to issue commendations to the provincial and municipal governments.

Regarding Mass Literacy Education and the Literacy Movement:

(1) Drafting regulations for the compulsory education of the masses by year and region; (2) Supervising the educational administrative organs of the capital to prepare for the trial implementation of compulsory education for the masses in the next year; (3) Formulating the organizational content, curriculum standards, and teaching methods of mass education teacher training institutions; (4) Urging each province and city to select prosperous or important townships to establish experimental zones and promote mass education and its related undertakings before the universal implementation of compulsory education for the masses; (5) Promoting and rewarding private organizations for conducting mass education experimental projects; (6) Strictly supervising the implementation of the adult literacy education plan after it is issued and promulgated by the Central Government; (7) Planning methods for training central mass literacy instructors; (8) Stipulating methods for the service and compensation of mass education administrative personnel; (9) Investigating the progress of mass education after the literacy movement in each province and city, and conducting strict assessments; (10) Formulating methods for promoting overseas Chinese mass education; (11) Working with the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to promote the development and implementation of agricultural extension services; (12) Working with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to investigate the living conditions of merchants, apprentices, and laborers, and earnestly planning improvements in industrial and commercial supplementary education.

Regarding Promoting the National Phonetic Alphabet:

(1) Formulating methods for promoting the National Phonetic Alphabet in each province, city, and county; (2) Supervising each province, city, and county to establish committees for promoting the National Phonetic Alphabet and vigorously implementing promotional work; (3) Holding National Phonetic Alphabet training sessions for party and government organs in the capital; (4) Designating Mandarin schools in Shanghai and Beiping with successful track records to send personnel from the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to study the National Phonetic Alphabet, and after graduation, returning to each province and city to serve as publicity instructors and promoters; (5) Formulating methods for evaluating the promotion of the National Phonetic Alphabet, as well as regulations for government employees and the public to learn and teach the National Phonetic Alphabet.

Regarding Libraries, Museums, Education Halls, Public Lecture Halls, and Preservation of Documents and Antiquities:

(1) Organizing and studying the survey forms submitted by existing libraries in each province and city, and stipulating library equipment standards; (2) Clarifying and stipulating the nature and scope of independently established mass education halls and mixed organizations containing museums, lecture halls, libraries, and other departments; (3) Investigating the work and efficiency of public lecture halls or other lecture and publicity organizations and gatherings in each province and city, and compiling them for research and reference; (4) Supervising and rewarding the progress of scientific and antiquities investigation projects jointly organized by Chinese and foreign parties; (5) Working with the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Interior to strictly implement measures to prevent ancient books from leaving the country.

The Second Summer School organized by the Anhui Education Department this year has been running for two weeks since its opening. Everything is more perfect than the first summer school. General Resignation of Teachers in the Urban Area of Yangzhou 159

Due to the Large Reduction in Elementary School Funding

Xin Fang and 147 other elementary school teachers and staff in the urban area of Jiangdu County have jointly submitted a request to the Education Bureau for permission to resign and seek other livelihoods due to the recent promulgation by the Education Department of the outline for the preparation of education budgets for various counties, which greatly reduces funding for elementary schools, making it difficult to maintain their livelihoods. The original request is recorded as follows: "Submitting a request for resignation due to reduced salaries and difficult living conditions, in order to give way to the virtuous and capable. The education expenses of Jiangdu have always been strained, and the salaries of teachers and staff are at most about 3,000 yuan per month. Even if they are paid monthly without arrears, there is still concern that it will not be enough. Compared with the party's political program of increasing education funding and developing child-centered education, the difference is as great as the sky and the earth. We were hoping to gradually increase funding and raise salaries in the future to ensure the stability and enrichment of the foundation of elementary education. Unexpectedly, the Education Department of Jiangsu recently promulgated the outline for the preparation of education budgets for various counties, which greatly reduces funding for elementary schools, making the lives of elementary school teachers and staff in the county even more difficult. On the part of the Bureau, the orders from superiors are clear, and they must be followed. Even the teachers and staff of each school should educate for the sake of education and not haggle over every penny, disregarding the foundation of the country's cause. However, with the rising tide of money and salaries that have not been increased, we already feel extremely embarrassed. If we further reduce funding, what difficulties can we imagine? At the county education administrative meeting this time, there was also a resolution to temporarily maintain the status quo regarding the budget issue, and the Reorganization Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Department also submitted a request to increase the salaries of elementary school teachers, which is reasonable. Furthermore, a few days ago, four representatives were jointly elected by our colleagues to go to the province with the Bureau Director to state the situation of Jiangdu's education funding and the impossibility of reducing it to the Department. Section Chief Yang Li received them and said that the budget standards previously issued by the Department were not without the possibility of flexibility. If there are special circumstances in each county, they can be handled with discretion and flexibility, and the Department's order is based on the principle of not reducing individual salaries. The Department's intention to maintain the lives of teachers and staff can already be seen. Now, the Bureau is adhering to the Department's order and is determined to implement the new budget. Our colleagues cannot deliberately violate the Department's order, nor can we disregard the safety of our lives. After repeated consideration, we are deeply afraid that our lack of focus will affect the development of our careers. Therefore, we all resign to give way to the virtuous and capable. We beg you to approve our resignation and hope that the salaries owed for each month will be paid off immediately to complete the procedures."

Relief Measures for Transferring Students from Unregistered and Closed Private Schools 160

Registration for Qualification Examinations Extended to August 10th

In order to facilitate the transfer of students and graduates from unregistered and closed private colleges and universities in Shanghai, the Ministry of Education is holding qualification examinations. Those who pass this qualification examination may apply for public and registered private colleges and universities according to their examination results and transfer to the corresponding grade. They will not be restricted by Article 4 of the University Regulations and Article 4 of the College Regulations to study in the final grade and take the exams. Students should register with the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau on time (the registration period was originally scheduled to end on July 31st, but it has been extended to August 10th). The examination regulations can be obtained from the Bureau by letter. (The examination was originally scheduled for August 7th, 8th, and 9th, but the examination venue is now the Jiaotong University. If the classrooms do not affect the time, it is planned to start the examination on August 17th.) When registering, applicants should submit a resume, a high school graduation certificate, a college graduation certificate or a study certificate. If there is a service certificate, it should also be submitted, along with two recent four-inch photos and an examination fee of one yuan. After the registration deadline, the official examination date and location will be announced. The specialized subjects for the examination will be announced seven days before the examination.
